    21	impl WriteTransformingVisitor<'_> {
    22	    pub fn get_array_member(&self, array_name: Symbol, index: &Expression) -> Option<Identifier> {
    23	        let members = self.array_members.get(&array_name)?;
    24	        let Expression::Literal(lit) = index else {
    25	            panic!("Const propagation should have ensured this is a literal.");
    26	        };
    27	        let index = lit
    28	            .as_u32()
    29	            .expect("Const propagation should have ensured this is in range, and consequently a valid u32.")
    30	            as usize;
    31	        Some(members[index])
    32	    }
    33	
    34	    pub fn get_composite_member(&self, composite_name: Symbol, field_name: Symbol) -> Option<Identifier> {
    35	        let members = self.composite_members.get(&composite_name)?;
    36	        members.get(&field_name).cloned()
    37	    }
    38	}
    39	
    40	impl WriteTransformingVisitor<'_> {
    41	    fn reconstruct_identifier(&mut self, input: Identifier) -> (Expression, Vec<Statement>) {
    42	        let ty = self.state.type_table.get(&input.id()).unwrap();
    43	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
    44	        if let Some(array_members) = self.array_members.get(&input.name) {
    45	            // Build the array expression from the members.
    46	            let id = self.state.node_builder.next_id();
    47	            self.state.type_table.insert(id, ty.clone());
    48	            let expr = ArrayExpression {
    49	                elements: array_members
    50	                    // This clone is unfortunate, but both `array_members` and the closure below borrow self.
    51	                    .clone()
    52	                    .iter()
    53	                    .map(|identifier| {
    54	                        let (expr, statements2) = self.reconstruct_identifier(*identifier);
    55	                        statements.extend(statements2);
    56	                        expr
    57	                    })
    58	                    .collect(),
    59	                span: Default::default(),
    60	                id,
    61	            };
    62	            let statement = AssignStatement {
    63	                place: Path::from(input).to_local().into(),
    64	                value: expr.into(),
    65	                span: Default::default(),
    66	                id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
    67	            };
    68	            statements.push(statement.into());
    69	            (Path::from(input).to_local().into(), statements)
    70	        } else if let Some(composite_members) = self.composite_members.get(&input.name) {
    71	            // Build the composite expression from the members.
    72	            let id = self.state.node_builder.next_id();
    73	            self.state.type_table.insert(id, ty.clone());
    74	            let Type::Composite(comp_type) = ty else {
    75	                panic!("The type of a composite init should be a composite.");
    76	            };
    77	            let expr = CompositeExpression {
    78	                const_arguments: Vec::new(), // All const arguments should have been resolved by now
    79	                members: composite_members
    80	                    // This clone is unfortunate, but both `composite_members` and the closure below borrow self.
    81	                    .clone()
    82	                    .iter()
    83	                    .map(|(field_name, ident)| {
    84	                        let (expr, statements2) = self.reconstruct_identifier(*ident);
    85	                        statements.extend(statements2);
    86	                        CompositeFieldInitializer {
    87	                            identifier: Identifier::new(*field_name, self.state.node_builder.next_id()),
    88	                            expression: Some(expr),
    89	                            span: Default::default(),
    90	                            id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
    91	                        }
    92	                    })
    93	                    .collect(),
    94	                path: comp_type.path,
    95	                span: Default::default(),
    96	                id,
    97	            };
    98	            let statement = AssignStatement {
    99	                place: Path::from(input).to_local().into(),
   100	                value: expr.into(),
   101	                span: Default::default(),
   102	                id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   103	            };
   104	            statements.push(statement.into());
   105	            (Path::from(input).to_local().into(), statements)
   106	        } else {
   107	            // This is not a composite or array whose members are written to, so there's nothing to do.
   108	            (Path::from(input).to_local().into(), Default::default())
   109	        }
   110	    }
   111	}
   112	
   113	impl AstReconstructor for WriteTransformingVisitor<'_> {
   114	    type AdditionalInput = ();
   115	    type AdditionalOutput = Vec<Statement>;
   116	
   117	    /* Expressions */
   118	    fn reconstruct_path(&mut self, input: Path, _additional: &()) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   119	        if let Some(name) = input.try_local_symbol() {
   120	            self.reconstruct_identifier(Identifier { name, span: input.span, id: input.id })
   121	        } else {
   122	            (input.into(), Default::default())
   123	        }
   124	    }
   125	
   126	    fn reconstruct_array_access(
   127	        &mut self,
   128	        input: ArrayAccess,
   129	        _additional: &(),
   130	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   131	        let Expression::Path(ref array_name) = input.array else {
   132	            panic!("SSA ensures that this is a Path.");
   133	        };
   134	        if let Some(member) = self.get_array_member(array_name.identifier().name, &input.index) {
   135	            self.reconstruct_identifier(member)
   136	        } else {
   137	            (input.into(), Default::default())
   138	        }
   139	    }
   140	
   141	    fn reconstruct_member_access(
   142	        &mut self,
   143	        input: MemberAccess,
   144	        _additional: &(),
   145	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   146	        let Expression::Path(ref composite_name) = input.inner else {
   147	            panic!("SSA ensures that this is a Path.");
   148	        };
   149	        if let Some(member) = self.get_composite_member(composite_name.identifier().name, input.name.name) {
   150	            self.reconstruct_identifier(member)
   151	        } else {
   152	            (input.into(), Default::default())
   153	        }
   154	    }
   155	
   156	    // The rest of the methods below don't do anything but traverse - we only modify their default implementations
   157	    // to combine the `Vec<Statement>` outputs.
   158	
   159	    fn reconstruct_intrinsic(
   160	        &mut self,
   161	        mut input: IntrinsicExpression,
   162	        _additional: &Self::AdditionalInput,
   163	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   164	        input.type_parameters =
   165	            input.type_parameters.into_iter().map(|(ty, span)| (self.reconstruct_type(ty).0, span)).collect();
   166	        input.input_types =
   167	            input.input_types.into_iter().map(|(mode, ty, span)| (mode, self.reconstruct_type(ty).0, span)).collect();
   168	        input.return_types =
   169	            input.return_types.into_iter().map(|(mode, ty, span)| (mode, self.reconstruct_type(ty).0, span)).collect();
   170	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
   171	        for arg in input.arguments.iter_mut() {
   172	            let (expr, statements2) = self.reconstruct_expression(std::mem::take(arg), &());
   173	            statements.extend(statements2);
   174	            *arg = expr;
   175	        }
   176	        (input.into(), statements)
   177	    }
   178	
   179	    fn reconstruct_tuple_access(
   180	        &mut self,
   181	        _input: TupleAccess,
   182	        _additional: &(),
   183	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   184	        panic!("`TupleAccess` should not be in the AST at this point.");
   185	    }
   186	
   187	    fn reconstruct_array(
   188	        &mut self,
   189	        mut input: ArrayExpression,
   190	        _additional: &(),
   191	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   192	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
   193	        for element in input.elements.iter_mut() {
   194	            let (expr, statements2) = self.reconstruct_expression(std::mem::take(element), &());
   195	            statements.extend(statements2);
   196	            *element = expr;
   197	        }
   198	        (input.into(), statements)
   199	    }
   200	
   201	    fn reconstruct_binary(
   202	        &mut self,
   203	        input: BinaryExpression,
   204	        _additional: &(),
   205	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   206	        let (left, mut statements) = self.reconstruct_expression(input.left, &());
   207	        let (right, statements2) = self.reconstruct_expression(input.right, &());
   208	        statements.extend(statements2);
   209	        (BinaryExpression { left, right, ..input }.into(), statements)
   210	    }
   211	
   212	    fn reconstruct_call(
   213	        &mut self,
   214	        mut input: CallExpression,
   215	        _additional: &(),
   216	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   217	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
   218	        for arg in input.arguments.iter_mut() {
   219	            let (expr, statements2) = self.reconstruct_expression(std::mem::take(arg), &());
   220	            statements.extend(statements2);
   221	            *arg = expr;
   222	        }
   223	        (input.into(), statements)
   224	    }
   225	
   226	    fn reconstruct_cast(&mut self, input: CastExpression, _additional: &()) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   227	        let (expression, statements) = self.reconstruct_expression(input.expression, &());
   228	        (CastExpression { expression, ..input }.into(), statements)
   229	    }
   230	
   231	    fn reconstruct_composite_init(
   232	        &mut self,
   233	        mut input: CompositeExpression,
   234	        _additional: &(),
   235	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   236	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
   237	        for member in input.members.iter_mut() {
   238	            assert!(member.expression.is_some());
   239	            let (expr, statements2) = self.reconstruct_expression(member.expression.take().unwrap(), &());
   240	            statements.extend(statements2);
   241	            member.expression = Some(expr);
   242	        }
   243	
   244	        (input.into(), statements)
   245	    }
   246	
   247	    fn reconstruct_err(
   248	        &mut self,
   249	        _input: leo_ast::ErrExpression,
   250	        _additional: &(),
   251	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   252	        std::panic!("`ErrExpression`s should not be in the AST at this phase of compilation.")
   253	    }
   254	
   255	    fn reconstruct_literal(
   256	        &mut self,
   257	        input: leo_ast::Literal,
   258	        _additional: &(),
   259	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   260	        (input.into(), Default::default())
   261	    }
   262	
   263	    fn reconstruct_ternary(
   264	        &mut self,
   265	        input: TernaryExpression,
   266	        _additional: &(),
   267	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   268	        let (condition, mut statements) = self.reconstruct_expression(input.condition, &());
   269	        let (if_true, statements2) = self.reconstruct_expression(input.if_true, &());
   270	        let (if_false, statements3) = self.reconstruct_expression(input.if_false, &());
   271	        statements.extend(statements2);
   272	        statements.extend(statements3);
   273	        (TernaryExpression { condition, if_true, if_false, ..input }.into(), statements)
   274	    }
   275	
   276	    fn reconstruct_tuple(
   277	        &mut self,
   278	        input: leo_ast::TupleExpression,
   279	        _additional: &(),
   280	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   281	        // This should ony appear in a return statement.
   282	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
   283	        let elements = input
   284	            .elements
   285	            .into_iter()
   286	            .map(|element| {
   287	                let (expr, statements2) = self.reconstruct_expression(element, &());
   288	                statements.extend(statements2);
   289	                expr
   290	            })
   291	            .collect();
   292	        (TupleExpression { elements, ..input }.into(), statements)
   293	    }
   294	
   295	    fn reconstruct_unary(
   296	        &mut self,
   297	        input: leo_ast::UnaryExpression,
   298	        _additional: &(),
   299	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   300	        let (receiver, statements) = self.reconstruct_expression(input.receiver, &());
   301	        (UnaryExpression { receiver, ..input }.into(), statements)
   302	    }
   303	
   304	    fn reconstruct_unit(
   305	        &mut self,
   306	        input: leo_ast::UnitExpression,
   307	        _additional: &(),
   308	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   309	        (input.into(), Default::default())
   310	    }
   311	
   312	    /* Statements */
   313	    /// This is the only reconstructing function where we do anything other than traverse and combine statements,
   314	    /// by calling `reconstruct_assign_place` and `reconstruct_assign_recurse`.
   315	    fn reconstruct_assign(&mut self, input: AssignStatement) -> (Statement, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   316	        let (value, mut statements) = self.reconstruct_expression(input.value, &());
   317	        let place = self.reconstruct_assign_place(input.place);
   318	        self.reconstruct_assign_recurse(place, value, &mut statements);
   319	        (Statement::dummy(), statements)
   320	    }
   321	
   322	    fn reconstruct_assert(&mut self, input: leo_ast::AssertStatement) -> (Statement, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   323	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
   324	        let stmt = AssertStatement {
   325	            variant: match input.variant {
   326	                AssertVariant::Assert(expr) => {
   327	                    let (expr, statements2) = self.reconstruct_expression(expr, &());
   328	                    statements.extend(statements2);
   329	                    AssertVariant::Assert(expr)
   330	                }
   331	                AssertVariant::AssertEq(left, right) => {
   332	                    let (left, statements2) = self.reconstruct_expression(left, &());
   333	                    statements.extend(statements2);
   334	                    let (right, statements3) = self.reconstruct_expression(right, &());
   335	                    statements.extend(statements3);
   336	                    AssertVariant::AssertEq(left, right)
   337	                }
   338	                AssertVariant::AssertNeq(left, right) => {
   339	                    let (left, statements2) = self.reconstruct_expression(left, &());
   340	                    statements.extend(statements2);
   341	                    let (right, statements3) = self.reconstruct_expression(right, &());
   342	                    statements.extend(statements3);
   343	                    AssertVariant::AssertNeq(left, right)
   344	                }
   345	            },
   346	            ..input
   347	        }
   348	        .into();
   349	        (stmt, Default::default())
   350	    }
   351	
   352	    fn reconstruct_block(&mut self, block: Block) -> (Block, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   353	        let mut statements = Vec::with_capacity(block.statements.len());
   354	
   355	        // Reconstruct the statements in the block, accumulating any additional statements.
   356	        for statement in block.statements {
   357	            let (reconstructed_statement, additional_statements) = self.reconstruct_statement(statement);
   358	            statements.extend(additional_statements);
   359	            if !reconstructed_statement.is_empty() {
   360	                statements.push(reconstructed_statement);
   361	            }
   362	        }
   363	
   364	        (Block { statements, ..block }, Default::default())
   365	    }
   366	
   367	    fn reconstruct_definition(&mut self, mut input: DefinitionStatement) -> (Statement, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
   368	        let (value, mut statements) = self.reconstruct_expression(input.value, &());
   369	        input.value = value;
   370	        match input.place.clone() {
   371	            DefinitionPlace::Single(identifier) => {
   372	                statements.push(input.into());
   373	                self.define_variable_members(identifier, &mut statements);
   374	            }
   375	            DefinitionPlace::Multiple(identifiers) => {
   376	                statements.push(input.into());
   377	                for &identifier in identifiers.iter() {
   378	                    self.define_variable_members(identifier, &mut statements);
   379	                }
   380	            }
   381	        }
   382	        (Statement::dummy(), statements)
   383	    }
   384

   386	        let (expression, statements) = self.reconstruct_ex<response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you.     41	/// This visitor associates a variable for each member of a composite or array that is
    42	/// written to. Whenever a member of the composite or array is written to, we change the
    43	/// assignment to access the variable instead. Whenever the composite or array itself
    44	/// is accessed, we first rebuild the composite or array from its variables.
    45	pub struct WriteTransformingVisitor<'a> {
    46	    pub state: &'a mut CompilerState,
    47	
    48	    /// For any composite whose members are written to, a map of its field names to variables
    49	    /// corresponding to the members.
    50	    pub composite_members: IndexMap<Symbol, IndexMap<Symbol, Identifier>>,
    51	
    52	    /// For any array whose members are written to, a vec containing the variables for each index.
    53	    pub array_members: IndexMap<Symbol, Vec<Identifier>>,
    54	
    55	    pub program: Symbol,
    56	}
    57	
    58	impl<'a> WriteTransformingVisitor<'a> {
    59	    pub fn new(state: &'a mut CompilerState, program: &Program) -> Self {
    60	        let visitor = WriteTransformingVisitor {
    61	            state,
    62	            composite_members: Default::default(),
    63	            array_members: Default::default(),
    64	            program: Symbol::intern(""),
    65	        };
    66	
    67	        // We need to do an initial pass through the AST to identify all arrays and composites that are written to.
    68	        let mut wtf = WriteTransformingFiller(visitor);
    69	        wtf.fill(program);
    70	        wtf.0
    71	    }
    72	
    73	    /// If `name` is a composite or array whose members are written to, make
    74	    /// `DefinitionStatement`s for each of its variables that will correspond to
    75	    /// the members. Note that we create them for all members; unnecessary ones
    76	    /// will be removed by DCE.
    77	    pub fn define_variable_members(&mut self, name: Identifier, accumulate: &mut Vec<Statement>) {
    78	        // The `cloned` here and in the branch below are unfortunate but we need
    79	        // to mutably borrow `self` again below.
    80	        if let Some(members) = self.array_members.get(&name.name).cloned() {
    81	            for (i, member) in members.iter().cloned().enumerate() {
    82	                // Create a definition for each array index.
    83	                let index = Literal::integer(
    84	                    IntegerType::U8,
    85	                    i.to_string(),
    86	                    Default::default(),
    87	                    self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
    88	                );
    89	                self.state.type_table.insert(index.id(), Type::Integer(IntegerType::U32));
    90	                let access = ArrayAccess {
    91	                    array: Path::from(name).to_local().into(),
    92	                    index: index.into(),
    93	                    span: Default::default(),
    94	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
    95	                };
    96	                self.state.type_table.insert(access.id(), self.state.type_table.get(&member.id()).unwrap().clone());
    97	                let def = DefinitionStatement {
    98	                    place: DefinitionPlace::Single(member),
    99	                    type_: None,
   100	                    value: access.into(),
   101	                    span: Default::default(),
   102	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   103	                };
   104	                accumulate.push(def.into());
   105	                // And recurse - maybe its members are also written to.
   106	                self.define_variable_members(member, accumulate);
   107	            }
   108	        } else if let Some(members) = self.composite_members.get(&name.name) {
   109	            for (&field_name, &member) in members.clone().iter() {
   110	                // Create a definition for each field.
   111	                let access = MemberAccess {
   112	                    inner: Path::from(name).to_local().into(),
   113	                    name: Identifier::new(field_name, self.state.node_builder.next_id()),
   114	                    span: Default::default(),
   115	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   116	                };
   117	                self.state.type_table.insert(access.id(), self.state.type_table.get(&member.id()).unwrap().clone());
   118	                let def = DefinitionStatement {
   119	                    place: DefinitionPlace::Single(member),
   120	                    type_: None,
   121	                    value: access.into(),
   122	                    span: Default::default(),
   123	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   124	                };
   125	                accumulate.push(def.into());
   126	                // And recurse - maybe its members are also written to.
   127	                self.define_variable_members(member, accumulate);
   128	            }
   129	        }
   130	    }
   131	
   132	    /// If we're assigning to a composite or array member, find the variable name we're actually writing to,
   133	    /// recursively if necessary.
   134	    /// That is, if we have
   135	    /// `arr[0u32][1u32] = ...`,
   136	    /// we find the corresponding variable `arr_0_1`.
   137	    pub fn reconstruct_assign_place(&mut self, input: Expression) -> Identifier {
   138	        use Expression::*;
   139	        match input {
   140	            ArrayAccess(array_access) => {
   141	                let identifier = self.reconstruct_assign_place(array_access.array);
   142	                self.get_array_member(identifier.name, &array_access.index).expect("We have visited all array writes.")
   143	            }
   144	            Path(path) => leo_ast::Identifier { name: path.identifier().name, span: path.span, id: path.id },
   145	            MemberAccess(member_access) => {
   146	                let identifier = self.reconstruct_assign_place(member_access.inner);
   147	                self.get_composite_member(identifier.name, member_access.name.name)
   148	                    .expect("We have visited all composites writes.")
   149	            }
   150	            TupleAccess(_) => panic!("TupleAccess writes should have been removed by Destructuring"),
   151	            _ => panic!("Type checking should have ensured there are no other places for assignments"),
   152	        }
   153	    }
   154	
   155	    /// If we're assigning to a composite or array, create assignments to the individual members, if applicable.
   156	    pub fn reconstruct_assign_recurse(&self, place: Identifier, value: Expression, accumulate: &mut Vec<Statement>) {
   157	        if let Some(array_members) = self.array_members.get(&place.name) {
   158	            if let Expression::Array(value_array) = value {
   159	                // This was an assignment like
   160	                // `arr = [a, b, c];`
   161	                // Change it to this:
   162	                // `arr_0 = a; arr_1 = b; arr_2 = c`
   163	                for (&member, rhs_element) in array_members.iter().zip(value_array.elements) {
   164	                    self.reconstruct_assign_recurse(member, rhs_element, accumulate);
   165	                }
   166	            } else {
   167	                // This was an assignment like
   168	                // `arr = x;`
   169	                // Change it to this:
   170	                // `arr = x; arr_0 = x[0]; arr_1 = x[1]; arr_2 = x[2];`
   171	                let one_assign = AssignStatement {
   172	                    place: Path::from(place).to_local().into(),
   173	                    value,
   174	                    span: Default::default(),
   175	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   176	                }
   177	                .into();
   178	                accumulate.push(one_assign);
   179	                for (i, &member) in array_members.iter().enumerate() {
   180	                    let access = ArrayAccess {
   181	                        array: Path::from(place).to_local().into(),
   182	                        index: Literal::integer(
   183	                            IntegerType::U32,
   184	                            format!("{i}u32"),
   185	                            Default::default(),
   186	                            self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   187	                        )
   188	                        .into(),
   189	                        span: Default::default(),
   190	                        id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   191	                    };
   192	                    self.reconstruct_assign_recurse(member, access.into(), accumulate);
   193	                }
   194	            }
   195	        } else if let Some(composite_members) = self.composite_members.get(&place.name) {
   196	            if let Expression::Composite(value_composite) = value {
   197	                // This was an assignment like
   198	                // `struc = S { field0: a, field1: b };`
   199	                // Change it to this:
   200	                // `struc_field0 = a; struc_field1 = b;`
   201	                for initializer in value_composite.members.into_iter() {
   202	                    let member_name =
   203	                        composite_members.get(&initializer.identifier.name).expect("Member should exist.");
   204	                    let rhs_expression =
   205	                        initializer.expression.expect("This should have been normalized to have a value.");
   206	                    self.reconstruct_assign_recurse(*member_name, rhs_expression, accumulate);
   207	                }
   208	            } else {
   209	                // This was an assignment like
   210	                // `struc = x;`
   211	                // Change it to this:
   212	                // `struc = x; struc_field0 = x.field0; struc_field1 = x.field1;`
   213	                let one_assign = AssignStatement {
   214	                    place: Path::from(place).to_local().into(),
   215	                    value,
   216	                    span: Default::default(),
   217	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   218	                }
   219	                .into();
   220	                accumulate.push(one_assign);
   221	                for (field, member_name) in composite_members.iter() {
   222	                    let access = MemberAccess {
   223	                        inner: Path::from(place).to_local().into(),
   224	                        name: Identifier::new(*field, self.state.node_builder.next_id()),
   225	                        span: Default::default(),
   226	                        id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   227	                    };
   228	                    if let Some(member_type) = self.state.type_table.get(&member_name.id) {
   229	                        self.state.type_table.insert(access.id, member_type);
   230	                    }
   231	                    self.reconstruct_assign_recurse(*member_name, access.into(), accumulate);
   232	                }
   233	            }
   234	        } else {
   235	            let stmt = AssignStatement {
   236	                value,
   237	                place: Path::from(place).to_local().into(),
   238	                id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   239	                span: Default::default(),
   240	            }
   241	            .into();
   242	            accumulate.push(stmt);
   243	        }
   244	    }
   245	}
   246	
   247	struct WriteTransformingFiller<'a>(WriteTransformingVisitor<'a>);
   248	
   249	impl AstVisitor for WriteTransformingFiller<'_> {
   250	    type AdditionalInput = ();
   251	    type Output = ();
   252	
   253	    /* Expressions */
   254	    fn visit_expression(&mut self, _input: &Expression, _additional: &Self::AdditionalInput) -> Self::Output {}
   255	
   256	    /* Statements */
   257	    fn visit_assign(&mut self, input: &AssignStatement) {
   258	        self.access_recurse(&input.place);
   259	    }
   260	}
   261	
   262	impl WriteTransformingFiller<'_> {
   263	    fn fill(&mut self, program: &Program) {
   264	        for stub in program.stubs.iter() {
   265	            if let (_, Stub::FromLeo { program, .. }) = stub {
   266	                self.fill(program);
   267	            }
   268	        }
   269	        for (_, module) in program.modules.iter() {
   270	            self.0.program = module.program_name;
   271	            for (_, function) in module.functions.iter() {
   272	                self.visit_block(&function.block);
   273	            }
   274	        }
   275	        for (_, scope) in program.program_scopes.iter() {
   276	            for (_, function) in scope.functions.iter() {
   277	                self.0.program = scope.program_id.as_symbol();
   278	                self.visit_block(&function.block);
   279	            }
   280	        }
   281	    }
   282	
   283	    /// Find assignments to arrays and composites and populate `array_members` and `composite_members` with new
   284	    /// variables names.
   285	    fn access_recurse(&mut self, place: &Expression) -> Identifier {
   286	        match place {
   287	            Expression::Path(path) => Identifier { name: path.identifier().name, span: path.span, id: path.id },
   288	            Expression::ArrayAccess(array_access) => {
   289	                let array_name = self.access_recurse(&array_access.array);
   290	                let members = self.0.array_members.entry(array_name.name).or_insert_with(|| {
   291	                    let ty = self.0.state.type_table.get(&array_access.array.id()).unwrap();
   292	                    let Type::Array(arr) = ty else { panic!("Type checking should have prevented this.") };
   293	                    (0..arr.length.as_u32().expect("length should be known at this point"))
   294	                        .map(|i| {
   295	                            let id = self.0.state.node_builder.next_id();
   296	                            let symbol = self.0.state.assigner.unique_symbol(format_args!("{array_name}#{i}"), "$");
   297	                            self.0.state.type_table.insert(id, arr.element_type().clone());
   298	                            Identifier::new(symbol, id)
   299	                        })
   300	                        .collect()
   301	                });
   302	                let Expression::Literal(lit) = &array_access.index else {
   303	                    panic!("Const propagation should have ensured this is a literal.");
   304	                };
   305	                members[lit
   306	                    .as_u32()
   307	                    .expect("Const propagation should have ensured this is in range, and consequently a valid u32.")
   308	                    as usize]
   309	            }
   310	            Expression::MemberAccess(member_access) => {
   311	                let composite_name = self.access_recurse(&member_access.inner);
   312	                let members = self.0.composite_members.entry(composite_name.name).or_insert_with(|| {
   313	                    let ty = self.0.state.type_table.get(&member_access.inner.id()).unwrap();
   314	                    let Type::Composite(comp) = ty else {
   315	                        panic!("Type checking should have prevented this.");
   316	                    };
   317	                    let composite_location = comp.path.expect_global_location();
   318	                    let composite = self
   319	                        .0
   320	                        .state
   321	                        .symbol_table
   322	                        .lookup_struct(self.0.program, composite_location)
   323	                        .or_else(|| self.0.state.symbol_table.lookup_record(self.0.program, composite_location))
   324	                        .unwrap();
   325	                    composite
   326	                        .members
   327	                        .iter()
   328	                        .map(|member| {
   329	                            let name = member.name();
   330	                            let id = self.0.state.node_builder.next_id();
   331	                            let symbol =
   332	                                self.0.state.assigner.unique_symbol(format_args!("{composite_name}#{name}"), "$");
   333	                            self.0.state.type_table.insert(id, member.type_.clone());
   334	                            (member.name(), Identifier::new(symbol, id))
   335	                        })
   336	                        .collect()
   337	                });
   338	                *members.get(&member_access.name.name).expect("Type checking should have ensured this is valid.")

```rust

    IntegerType::U8,
    i.to_string(),
```

This creates a `U8` literal with the index `i` as a string. But if the array length is > 256, `i` will be >= 256, which can't be represented as `u8`. This is then passed through the code and eventually hits `literal_to_value` which calls `u8::from_str_by_radix` and panics with `PosOverflow`.

```rust

    IntegerType::U32,
    format!("{i}u32"),
```

That uses `U32` which is fine. The problem is specifically with `IntegerType::U8` at line 84.

Let me also check line 83-88 more carefully. The index literal is created with `IntegerType::U8` but then at line 89, the type table entry is set to `Type::Integer(IntegerType::U32)`. So there's a mismatch - the literal says it's a `u8` but the type table says `u32`. When `literal_to_value` is later called on this literal, it uses the literal's own type (U8) to parse, and if the value is >= 256, it panics.

Let me trace where this literal flows. The `define_variable_members` function creates an `ArrayAccess` with the index literal. This goes into a `DefinitionStatement` which gets pushed into the AST. Then later passes (SSA const propagation, etc.) will process these literals.

The issue is that in `write_transforming/visitor.rs` at lines 83-88, when creating index literals for array member accesses, the code uses `IntegerType::U8` but the value may exceed 255 (for arrays with length > 256). Then later, SSA const propagation tries to parse this literal as a `u8` and panics.

Let me fix the issue. The fix should change `IntegerType::U8` to something that can handle larger array sizes. Looking at line 182-187 in the same file, the second case uses `IntegerType::U32`. The fix should change line 84 from `IntegerType::U8` to `IntegerType::U32` (or at least `U16` for arrays up to 65536).

But wait, there might be a deeper issue. Let me look at line 83-88 more carefully:

```rust
let index = Literal::integer(
    IntegerType::U8,
    i.to_string(),
    Default::default(),
    self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
);
self.state.type_table.insert(index.id(), Type::Integer(IntegerType::U32));
```

The type table says `U32` but the literal says `U8`. When the SSA const propagation pass encounters this literal and calls `literal_to_value`, it goes to line 162-164 of evaluate.rs:

```rust
LiteralVariant::Integer(IntegerType::U8, s, ..) => {
    let s = s.replace("_", "");
    u8::from_str_by_radix(&s).expect("Parsing guarantees this works.").into()
}
```

So the literal's own type (U8) is used for parsing, not the type table. That's the bug.

The simplest fix is to change `IntegerType::U8` to `IntegerType::U32` in `write_transforming/visitor.rs` line 84, since the type table already says `U32`.

But I should also check: is there another place where this same issue could arise? Let me check line 182-187 again:

```rust
index: Literal::integer(
    IntegerType::U32,
    format!("{i}u32"),
    Default::default(),
    self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
)
```

That already uses `U32`. Good.

But there's also the `as_u32()` calls in `write_transforming/ast.rs` line 27-29 and `write_transforming/visitor.rs` line 305-308. These call `lit.as_u32()` which should work fine regardless of the literal type (it handles U8, U16, U32, etc.).

Now let me make the fix:

Now, let me think more broadly about whether there could be other places where a similar issue could arise. The PR description says:

> SSA const propagation pass synthesizes a literal in the index type whose value cannot be represented in `u8`.

But actually the root cause is in the `write_transforming` pass which creates `U8` literals for array indices even when the array length exceeds 256. The literal gets stored, then later SSA const propagation tries to parse it and panics.

However, I should also check: is there any other path that could create a similar situation? Let me look at the `const_propagation/ast.rs` at line 152-155:

```rust
let len = array_ty.length.as_u32();
if let Some(len) = len {
    let index_in_bounds = matches!(index_value.as_u32(), Some(index) if index < len);
```

This uses `as_u32()` which is safe. And line 173:
```rust
.array_index(index_value.as_u32().unwrap() as usize)
```

This is also safe because `as_u32()` handles all integer types.

But what about the `ssa_const_propagation/ast.rs` at line 186:
```rust
array_value.array_index(index_value.as_u32().unwrap() as usize).expect("We already checked bounds.");
```

This also uses `as_u32()` which is safe.

The issue was specifically the creation of the `U8` literal in `write_transforming/visitor.rs`. My fix changes it to `U32`, which can handle indices up to 2^32 - 1, far more than any practical array size.

But wait, I should also check if there's a similar issue in `write_transforming/visitor.rs` at line 293:

```rust

```

```rust
members[lit
    .as_u32()
    .expect("Const propagation should have ensured this is in range, and consequently a valid u32.")
    as usize]
```

This calls `lit.as_u32()` which works for all integer types.

So my fix is complete. Let me also think about whether the `literal_to_value` function itself should be more defensive. Looking at the code:

```rust
LiteralVariant::Integer(IntegerType::U8, s, ..) => {
    let s = s.replace("_", "");
    u8::from_str_by_radix(&s).expect("Parsing guarantees this works.").into()
}
```

The comment says "Parsing guarantees this works." But as we've seen, the parser can produce a U8 literal with a value that doesn't fit in u8 if the code in `write_transforming` creates one. The parser itself would never create such an invalid literal from source code, but other passes might synthesize them. 

I could also make `literal_to_value` more robust by returning an error instead of panicking. But the PR description says the fix should either make type checking emit a diagnostic or SSA use an index-type-agnostic representation. My fix addresses the root cause (the write transforming pass creating invalid U8 literals).

All good. Let me now think about whether there might be another approach that's more robust. The PR description says:

> Expected behavior: type checking emits a diagnostic (e.g., `index type too narrow for array length`), or SSA uses an index-type-agnostic representation, instead of panicking.

My fix is the second approach: use an index-type-agnostic representation (U32 instead of U8). The synthetic index literals generated by the compiler should always use a wide enough type.

But also, looking at the `literal_to_value` function, I think it would be good practice to replace the `.expect()` calls with proper error handling, so that if a similar issue occurs in the future, it would produce a proper error message instead of a panic. However, the PR description says the expected behavior is specifically about this case, and my fix addresses it.

Let me also check if there's a way to make `literal_to_value` more robust by using `halt2!` instead of `.expect()`:

Actually, looking at the code again, I notice that `literal_to_value` returns `Result<Value>`. The `.expect()` calls could be replaced with `map_err` or `halt2!` to return proper errors. But since the root cause is fixed, and the PR description doesn't require this change, I'll leave it as is. The existing `.expect()` is based on the assumption that the parser guarantees valid values, and my fix ensures that compiler-synthesized literals also have valid values.

When the array length exceeded 256 (the maximum value of `u8`), the index `i` would be >= 256, which cannot be represented as a `u8`. Later, the SSA const propagation pass would try to parse these literals via `literal_to_value`, which would panic with `ParseIntError { kind: PosOverflow }` when trying to parse a value like "256" as a `u8`.\n\n### Fix\n\nChanged the synthetic index literal from `IntegerType::U8` to `IntegerType::U32` in `crates/passes/src/write_transforming/visitor.rs` (line 84).
